# Analyzing Census Microdata

## PUMS and tidyverse

### Basic weight tabulation

``` r
library(tidycensus)
library(tidyverse)
```

    ## ── Attaching core tidyverse packages ──────────────────────── tidyverse 2.0.0 ──
    ## ✔ dplyr     1.1.4     ✔ readr     2.1.5
    ## ✔ forcats   1.0.0     ✔ stringr   1.5.1

    ## ✔ purrr     1.0.4

    ## ✖ dplyr::lag()    masks stats::lag()
    ## ℹ Use the conflicted package (<http://conflicted.r-lib.org/>) to force all conflicts to become errors

``` r
nm_pums <- get_pums(
  variables = c("SEX", "AGEP"),
  state = "NM",
  survey = "acs5",
  year = 2023,
  recode = T
)
```

### Group-wise tabulation

> How does rent burden vary by race/ethnicity and household type?

This requires obtaining data on rent burden (gross rent as percentage of
household income) with variable `GRPIP`; race and ethnicity with
variables `RAC1P` and `HISP`; and household type with variable `HHT`.

``` r
hh_variables <- c("PUMA", "GRPIP", "RAC1P", 
                  "HISP", "HHT")

nm_hh_data <- get_pums(
  variables = hh_variables,
  state = "NM",
  year = 2023,
  variables_filter = list(
    SPORDER = 1,
    TEN = 3  # Households paying cash rent
  )
)
```

``` r
nm_hh_recoded <- nm_hh_data |> 
  mutate(
    race_ethnicity = case_when(
      HISP != "01" ~ "Hispanic",
      HISP == "01" & RAC1P == "1" ~ "White",
      HISP == "01" & RAC1P == "2" ~ "Black",
      HISP == "01" & RAC1P == "3" ~ "Native",
      TRUE ~ "Other"
    ),
    married = case_when(
      HHT == "1" ~ "Married",
      TRUE ~ "Not married"
    )
  )

nm_hh_summary <- nm_hh_recoded |> 
  filter(race_ethnicity != "Other") |> 
  group_by(race_ethnicity, married) |> 
  summarize(
    prop_above_40 = sum(WGTP[GRPIP >= 40]) / sum(WGTP)
  )
```

    ## `summarise()` has grouped output by 'race_ethnicity'. You can override using
    ## the `.groups` argument.

``` r
nm_hh_summary
```

    ## # A tibble: 8 × 3
    ## # Groups:   race_ethnicity [4]
    ##   race_ethnicity married     prop_above_40
    ##   <chr>          <chr>               <dbl>
    ## 1 Black          Married             0.178
    ## 2 Black          Not married         0.435
    ## 3 Hispanic       Married             0.258
    ## 4 Hispanic       Not married         0.403
    ## 5 Native         Married             0.149
    ## 6 Native         Not married         0.363
    ## 7 White          Married             0.173
    ## 8 White          Not married         0.370

> 43.5% of unmarried black households pay over 40% of their incomes in
> gross rent

## Mapping PUMS data

``` r
library(tigris)
```

    ## To enable caching of data, set `options(tigris_use_cache = TRUE)`
    ## in your R script or .Rprofile.

``` r
library(tmap)
options(tigris_use_cache = T)

nm_pumas <- pumas("NM", year = 2020)

plot(nm_pumas$geometry)
```

![](10-AnalyzingCensusMicrodata_files/figure-gfm/unnamed-chunk-9-1.png)<!-- -->

> prepare data for map

``` r
nm_data_for_map <- nm_hh_recoded |> 
  group_by(race_ethnicity, married, PUMA) |> 
  summarise(
    percent_above_40 = 100 * (sum(WGTP[GRPIP >= 40]) / sum(WGTP))
  ) |> 
  filter(race_ethnicity == "Native",
         married == "Not married")
```

    ## `summarise()` has grouped output by 'race_ethnicity', 'married'. You can
    ## override using the `.groups` argument.

``` r
library(tmap)

joined_pumas <- nm_pumas |> 
  left_join(nm_data_for_map, by = c("PUMACE10" =  "PUMA"))

tm_shape(joined_pumas) +
  tm_polygons(col = "percent_above_40",
              palette = "Reds",
              title = "% rent-burdened\nunmarried Native households") +
  tm_layout(legend.outside = T,
            legend.outside.posistion = "right")
```

![](10-AnalyzingCensusMicrodata_files/figure-gfm/unnamed-chunk-11-1.png)<!-- -->

## Survey design and ACS PUMS

### Get data with replicate weights

In order to calculate std. errors and moes, a special formula must be
used involving *replicate weights* for each observation and *Successive
Difference Replication*.

> Download data with household replicate weights.
>
> Note that TEN is included, filtering must take place after the
> calculations are performed to ensure that they take into account the
> full structure.

``` r
nm_hh_replicate <- get_pums(
  variables = c("TEN", hh_variables),
  state = "NM",
  recode = T,
  year = 2023,
  variables_filter = list(
    SPORDER = 1
  ),
  rep_weights = "housing"
)
```

### Estimates and errors

``` r
nm_hh_svy |> 
  survey_count(PUMA, HHT_label) |> 
  head()
```

    ## # A tibble: 6 × 4
    ##   PUMA  HHT_label                                                        n  n_se
    ##   <chr> <ord>                                                        <dbl> <dbl>
    ## 1 00100 Married couple household                                      2174 226. 
    ## 2 00100 Other family household: Male householder, no spouse present    915 162. 
    ## 3 00100 Other family household: Female householder, no spouse prese…  3214 344. 
    ## 4 00100 Nonfamily household: Male householder: Living alone           1072 198. 
    ## 5 00100 Nonfamily household: Male householder: Not living alone        163  54.2
    ## 6 00100 Nonfamily household: Female householder: Living alone         1404 234.

> the survey object has its own functions for count and mean, for
> example.

``` r
nm_svy_summary <- nm_hh_svy |> 
  mutate(
    race_ethnicity = case_when(
      HISP != "01" ~ "Hispanic",
      HISP == "01" & RAC1P == "1" ~ "White",
      HISP == "01" & RAC1P == "2" ~ "Black",
      HISP == "01" & RAC1P == "3" ~ "Native",
      TRUE ~ "Other"
    ),
    married = case_when(
      HHT == "1" ~ "Married",
      TRUE ~ "Not married"
    ),
    above_40 = GRPIP >= 40
  ) |> 
  filter(race_ethnicity != "Other") |> 
  group_by(race_ethnicity, married) |> 
  summarize(
    prop_above_40 = survey_mean(above_40)
  )
head(nm_svy_summary)
```

    ## # A tibble: 6 × 4
    ## # Groups:   race_ethnicity [3]
    ##   race_ethnicity married     prop_above_40 prop_above_40_se
    ##   <chr>          <chr>               <dbl>            <dbl>
    ## 1 Black          Married             0.178           0.0633
    ## 2 Black          Not married         0.435           0.0407
    ## 3 Hispanic       Married             0.258           0.0223
    ## 4 Hispanic       Not married         0.403           0.0132
    ## 5 Native         Married             0.149           0.0378
    ## 6 Native         Not married         0.363           0.0263

### Convert standard errors to margins of error.

To convert standard errors to *margins of error* around the derived PUMS
estimates, analysts should multiply the standard errors by the following
coefficients:

- 90 percent confidence level: 1.645
- 95 percent confidence level: 1.96
- 99 percent confidence level: 2.576

``` r
nm_svy_summary_moe <- nm_svy_summary |> 
  mutate(prop_above_40_moe = prop_above_40_se * 1.645,
         label = paste(race_ethnicity, married, sep = ", "))


nm_svy_summary_moe |> 
  ggplot(aes(x = prop_above_40,
             y = reorder(label,
                         prop_above_40))) +
  geom_errorbar(aes(xmin = prop_above_40 - prop_above_40_moe,
                    xmax = prop_above_40 + prop_above_40_moe)) +
  geom_point(size = 3, color = "navy") +
  labs(title = "Rent burdened-households in New Mexico",
       x = "2018-2023 ACS estimate (from PUMS data)",
       y = "",
       caption = "Rent-burdened defined when gross rent is 40 percent or more\nof household income. Error bars represent a 90 percent confidence level.") +
  scale_x_continuous(labels = scales::percent) +
  theme_grey(base_size = 12)
```

## Modeling PUMS data

``` r
nm_pums_to_model <- get_pums(
    variables = c("PUMA", "SEX", "MIG",
                "AGEP", "SCHL", "WAGP", 
                "COW", "ESR", "MAR", "NOC"),
  state = "NM",
  survey = "acs5",
  year = 2023,
  rep_weights = "person"
)

MB     Downloading: 24 MB

### Data prep

The target variable is coded 0 or 1 since we will estimate a logistic
regression model with a binary outcome.

``` r
nm_pums_recoded <- nm_pums_to_model %>%
  mutate(
    emp_type = case_when(
      COW %in% c("1", "2") ~ "private",
      COW %in% c("3", "4", "5") ~ "public",
      TRUE ~ "self"
      ), 
    child = case_when(
      NOC > 0 ~ "yes",
      TRUE ~ "no"
    ),
    married = case_when(
      MAR == 1 ~ "yes",
      TRUE ~ "no"
    ),
    college = case_when(
      SCHL %in% as.character(21:24) ~ "yes",
      TRUE ~ "no"
    ),
    sex = case_when(
      SEX == 2 ~ "female",
      TRUE ~ "male"
    ),
    migrated = case_when(
      MIG == 1 ~ 0,
      TRUE ~ 1
    )
  )
```

> Focus on individuals aged 25-49 who are employed and have earned wages
> in the past year.

``` r
nm_model_svy <- nm_pums_recoded %>% 
  to_survey() %>%
  filter(
    ESR == 1,   # civilian employed
    WAGP > 0,   # earned wages last year
    AGEP >= 25,
    AGEP <= 49
  ) %>%
  rename(age = AGEP, wages = WAGP)
```

### Fit and evaluate

``` r
migration_model <- svyglm(
  formula = migrated ~ log(wages) + sex + age + emp_type + 
    child + married + college + PUMA,
  design = nm_model_svy,
  family = quasibinomial()
) 
```

``` r
summary(migration_model)
```
